<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The most accepted explanation is that Curaçao was the name by which the indigenous peoples of the island identified themselves, their autonym.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Early Spanish accounts support this theory, as they refer to the indigenous peoples as <i>Indios Curaçaos</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-curacao-nature_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-curacao-nature-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From 1525, the island was featured on Spanish maps as <i>Curaçote, Curasaote, Curasaore</i> and even <i>Curacaute</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> By the 17th century, it appeared on most maps as <i>Curaçao</i> or <i>Curazao.</i><sup id="cite_ref-curacao-nature_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-curacao-nature-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> On a map created by <a href="/wiki/Hieronymus_Cock" title="Hieronymus Cock">Hieronymus Cock</a> in 1562 in <a href="/wiki/Antwerp" title="Antwerp">Antwerp</a>, the island was referred to as <i>Qúracao.</i><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A persistent but undocumented story mentions that in the 16th and 17th centuries – the early years of European exploration – sailors on long voyages would often get <a href="/wiki/Scurvy" title="Scurvy">scurvy</a> from lack of <a href="/wiki/Vitamin_C" title="Vitamin C">vitamin C</a>. According to some accounts, either Portuguese or Spanish sailors who were ill were left on the island now known as Curaçao. When their ship returned, some had recovered, likely cured from scurvy after eating fruit with vitamin C. From then on, supposedly, the Portuguese referred to this as <i>Ilha da Curação</i> (Island of Healing)<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> or the Spanish as <i>Isla de la Curación</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Another explanation is that it is derived from the <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> word for heart (<i lang="pt"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cora%C3%A7%C3%A3o#Portuguese" class="extiw" title="wikt:coração">coração</a></i>), referring to the island as a centre in trade. An unstressed <i>o</i> in Continental Portuguese is usually pronounced [u], so the Portuguese word for heart, coração, is actually pronounced [kurɐsãw]. Spanish traders would have taken over the name as Curaçao, which was followed by the Dutch.<sup id="cite_ref-curacao-nature_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-curacao-nature-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> There is no evidence of the Portuguese reaching the island before the Spanish, however.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="History of Curaçao">History of Curaçao</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_and_Dependencies" title="Curaçao and Dependencies">Curaçao and Dependencies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Caribbean" title="Dutch Caribbean">Dutch Caribbean</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-colonial">Pre-colonial</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Pre-colonial">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1562_Americae-Gutierrez_map_10hrs-inn_Sth-Florida-Cuba-Spagnola-Benezuela-to-Lesser-Antilles.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/1562_Americae-Gutierrez_map_10hrs-inn_Sth-Florida-Cuba-Spagnola-Benezuela-to-Lesser-Antilles.jpg/220px-1562_Americae-Gutierrez_map_10hrs-inn_Sth-Florida-Cuba-Spagnola-Benezuela-to-Lesser-Antilles.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/1562_Americae-Gutierrez_map_10hrs-inn_Sth-Florida-Cuba-Spagnola-Benezuela-to-Lesser-Antilles.jpg/330px-1562_Americae-Gutierrez_map_10hrs-inn_Sth-Florida-Cuba-Spagnola-Benezuela-to-Lesser-Antilles.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/1562_Americae-Gutierrez_map_10hrs-inn_Sth-Florida-Cuba-Spagnola-Benezuela-to-Lesser-Antilles.jpg/440px-1562_Americae-Gutierrez_map_10hrs-inn_Sth-Florida-Cuba-Spagnola-Benezuela-to-Lesser-Antilles.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2660" data-file-height="2330" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1562_Americae-Gutierrez_map_10hrs-inn_Sth-Florida-Cuba-Spagnola-Benezuela-to-Lesser-Antilles.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map from 1562 with Curaçao indicated as Qúracao</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cura%C3%A7ao1836.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Cura%C3%A7ao1836.png/220px-Cura%C3%A7ao1836.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="183" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Cura%C3%A7ao1836.png/330px-Cura%C3%A7ao1836.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cf/Cura%C3%A7ao1836.png/440px-Cura%C3%A7ao1836.png 2x" data-file-width="2366" data-file-height="1964" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cura%C3%A7ao1836.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Curaçao in 1836</div></div></div>
<p>The original inhabitants of Curaçao were the <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">Arawak</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caquetio" title="Caquetio">Caquetio</a> Amerindians.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Their ancestors had migrated to the island from the mainland of South America, likely hundreds of years before Europeans arrived. They were believed to have migrated from the Amazon Basin.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arrival_of_Europeans">Arrival of Europeans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Arrival of Europeans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first Europeans recorded as seeing the island were members of a Spanish expedition under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Alonso_de_Ojeda" title="Alonso de Ojeda">Alonso de Ojeda</a> in 1499.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The Spaniards enslaved most of the Arawak for forced labour but paid little attention to the island itself.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1634, after the Netherlands achieved independence from Spain following the <a href="/wiki/Eighty_Years%27_War" title="Eighty Years&#39; War">Eighty Years' War</a>, Dutch colonists started to occupy the island.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">Dutch West India Company</a> founded the capital of Willemstad on the banks of an inlet called the Schottegat; this <a href="/wiki/Natural_harbour" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural harbour">natural harbour</a> proved to be an ideal place for trade. Commerce and shipping—and <a href="/wiki/Piracy_in_the_Caribbean" title="Piracy in the Caribbean">piracy</a>—became Curaçao's most important economic activities. Later, <a href="/wiki/Salt_mines" class="mw-redirect" title="Salt mines">salt mining</a> became a major industry, the mineral being a lucrative export at the time.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> From 1662 the Dutch West India Company made Curaçao a centre for the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a>, often bringing slaves from West Africa here for sale elsewhere in the Caribbean and on the mainland of South America.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sephardic_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Sephardic Jews">Sephardic Jews</a> with ancestors from the Iberian Peninsula settled here with the Dutch and in then-<a href="/wiki/Dutch_Brazil" title="Dutch Brazil">Dutch Brazil</a>; they have had a significant influence on the culture and economy of the island.<sup id="cite_ref-history_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Dutch_War" title="Franco-Dutch War">Franco-Dutch War</a> of 1672-78, Count <a href="/wiki/Jean_II_d%27Estr%C3%A9es" title="Jean II d&#39;Estrées">Jean II d'Estrées</a> planned to attack Curaçao. His fleet&#160;– 12 men of war, three fireships, two transports, a hospital ship, and 12 privateers&#160;– met with disaster, losing seven men-of-war and two other ships when they struck reefs off the <a href="/wiki/Las_Aves_archipelago" title="Las Aves archipelago">Las Aves archipelago</a>. They had made a serious navigational error, hitting the reefs on 11 May 1678, a week after setting sail from <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts" title="Saint Kitts">Saint Kitts</a>. Curaçao marked the events by a day of thanksgiving, celebrated for decades into the 18th century, to commemorate the island's escape.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dutch_colonial_rule">Dutch colonial rule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Dutch colonial rule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cura%C3%A7ao,_Broad_Street.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cura%C3%A7ao%2C_Broad_Street.jpg/220px-Cura%C3%A7ao%2C_Broad_Street.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cura%C3%A7ao%2C_Broad_Street.jpg/330px-Cura%C3%A7ao%2C_Broad_Street.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Cura%C3%A7ao%2C_Broad_Street.jpg/440px-Cura%C3%A7ao%2C_Broad_Street.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1745" data-file-height="1279" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cura%C3%A7ao,_Broad_Street.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Willemstad, 1885.</div></div></div>
<p>Many Dutch colonists grew affluent from the slave trade, building impressive colonial buildings in the capital of Willemstad; the city is now designated as a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>. Landhouses (former plantation estates) and West African style <i>kas di pal'i maishi</i> (former slave dwellings) are scattered all over the island.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In 1795, a major <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_Slave_Revolt_of_1795" title="Curaçao Slave Revolt of 1795">slave revolt</a> took place under the leaders <a href="/wiki/Tula_(Cura%C3%A7ao)" title="Tula (Curaçao)">Tula Rigaud</a>, Louis Mercier, Bastian Karpata, and Pedro Wakao. Up to 4,000 slaves on the northwest section of the island revolted, with more than 1,000 slaves taking part in extended gunfights. After a month, the slave owners suppressed the revolt.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luis_Bri%C3%B3n_2012_000.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Luis_Bri%C3%B3n_2012_000.jpg/220px-Luis_Bri%C3%B3n_2012_000.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Luis_Bri%C3%B3n_2012_000.jpg/330px-Luis_Bri%C3%B3n_2012_000.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Luis_Bri%C3%B3n_2012_000.jpg/440px-Luis_Bri%C3%B3n_2012_000.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="2480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luis_Bri%C3%B3n_2012_000.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Luis_Bri%C3%B3n" title="Luis Brión">Luis Brión</a>, a Curaçao-born Venezuelan admiral.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Willemstad_harbor.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Willemstad_harbor.jpg/220px-Willemstad_harbor.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Willemstad_harbor.jpg/330px-Willemstad_harbor.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Willemstad_harbor.jpg/440px-Willemstad_harbor.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Willemstad_harbor.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dutch architecture along <a href="/wiki/Willemstad" title="Willemstad">Willemstad</a>'s harbor.</div></div></div>
<p>Curaçao's proximity to South America resulted in interaction with cultures of the coastal areas more than a century after independence of Netherlands from Spain. Architectural similarities can be seen between the 19th-century parts of Willemstad and the nearby Venezuelan city of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Ana_de_Coro" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Ana de Coro">Coro</a> in <a href="/wiki/Falc%C3%B3n_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Falcón State">Falcón State</a>. The latter has also been designated a UNESCO World Heritage Site. Netherlands established economic ties with <a href="/wiki/Viceroyalty_of_New_Granada" title="Viceroyalty of New Granada">Viceroyalty of New Granada</a>, which included the present-day countries of <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>. In the 19th century, Curaçaoans such as <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Piar" title="Manuel Piar">Manuel Piar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Bri%C3%B3n" title="Luis Brión">Luis Brión</a> were prominently engaged in the wars of independence of Venezuela and <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>. Political refugees from the mainland (such as <a href="/wiki/Simon_Bolivar" class="mw-redirect" title="Simon Bolivar">Simon Bolivar</a>) regrouped in Curaçao.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Children from affluent Venezuelan families were educated on the island.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>During the 18th and 19th centuries, the British attacked the island several times, most notably in <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Cura%C3%A7ao_(1800)" title="Invasion of Curaçao (1800)">1800</a>, 1804, and the period from 1807 to 1815.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Stable Dutch rule returned in 1815 at the end of the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleonic wars">Napoleonic wars</a>, when the island was incorporated into the colony of <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_and_Dependencies" title="Curaçao and Dependencies">Curaçao and Dependencies</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the early 19th century, Portuguese and Lebanese migrated to Curaçao, attracted by the business opportunities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The Dutch abolished slavery in 1863, bringing a change in the economy with the shift to wage labor.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Some inhabitants of Curaçao emigrated to other islands, such as <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>, to work in <a href="/wiki/Sugar_plantations_in_the_Caribbean" title="Sugar plantations in the Caribbean">sugarcane plantations</a>. Other former slaves had nowhere to go and remained working for the plantation owner in the <a href="/wiki/Tenant_farmer" title="Tenant farmer">tenant farmer</a> system.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> This was an instituted order in which the former slave leased land from his former master; in exchange, the tenant promised to give up for rent most of his harvest to the former slave master. This system lasted until the beginning of the 20th century.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Historically, Dutch was not widely spoken on the island outside of colonial administration; its use increased in the late 19th and early 20th centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-Putte_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Putte-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Students on Curaçao, Aruba, and Bonaire were taught predominantly in Spanish until the late 17th century, when the British took Curaçao, Aruba, and Bonaire. Teaching of Spanish was restored when Dutch rule resumed in 1815. Also, efforts were made to introduce bilingual popular education in Dutch and Papiamentu in the late 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_and_21st_centuries">20th and 21st centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 20th and 21st centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When oil was discovered in the Venezuelan <a href="/wiki/Maracaibo_Basin" title="Maracaibo Basin">Maracaibo Basin</a> town of Mene Grande in 1914, the economic fortunes of the island were dramatically altered. In the early years, both Shell and <a href="/wiki/Exxon" title="Exxon">Exxon</a> held drilling concessions in Venezuela, which ensured a constant supply of crude oil to the refineries in Aruba and Curaçao. Crude oil production in Venezuela was inexpensive. The integrated companies Shell and Exxon controlled the entire industry from pumping, transporting, and refining to marketing the end product. The refineries on Aruba and Curaçao operated in global markets and were profitable partly because of the margin between the production costs of crude oil and the revenues realized on products. This provided a safety net for losses incurred through inefficiency or excessive operating costs at the refineries.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1929 Curaçao was attacked by Venezuelan rebel commander <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Sim%C3%B3n_Urbina" title="Rafael Simón Urbina">Rafael Simón Urbina</a>, who kidnapped the governor <a href="/w/index.php?title=Leonardus_Albertus_Fruytier&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Leonardus Albertus Fruytier (page does not exist)">Leonardus Albertus Fruytier</a>. As a result of this incident the Dutch increased their military presence on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-mindef_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mindef-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1954 Curaçao was joined with the other Dutch colonies in the Caribbean into the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</a>. Discontent with Curaçao’s seemingly subordinate relationship to the Netherlands, coupled with ongoing racial discrimination and a rise in unemployment owing to layoffs in the oil industry, led to an <a href="/wiki/1969_Cura%C3%A7ao_uprising" title="1969 Curaçao uprising">outbreak of rioting</a> in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The riots resulted in two deaths, many injuries and severe damage to Willemstad. As a result the Dutch government introduced far-reaching reforms, allowing Afro-Curaçaoans greater influence in the islands's political and economic life, and raising the prestige of the local language Papiamento.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dutch_soldier,_1969_Cura%C3%A7ao_uprising.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ad/Dutch_soldier%2C_1969_Cura%C3%A7ao_uprising.png/220px-Dutch_soldier%2C_1969_Cura%C3%A7ao_uprising.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="180" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ad/Dutch_soldier%2C_1969_Cura%C3%A7ao_uprising.png/330px-Dutch_soldier%2C_1969_Cura%C3%A7ao_uprising.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/ad/Dutch_soldier%2C_1969_Cura%C3%A7ao_uprising.png 2x" data-file-width="352" data-file-height="288" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dutch_soldier,_1969_Cura%C3%A7ao_uprising.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Dutch soldier on patrol in Willemstad following the 1969 riots</div></div></div>
<p>Curaçao experienced an economic downturn in the early 1980s. Shell's refinery on Curaçao operated with significant losses from 1975 to 1979, and again from 1982 to 1985. Persistent losses, global <a href="/wiki/Overproduction" title="Overproduction">overproduction</a>, stronger competition, and low market expectations threatened the future of the Shell refinery in Curaçao. In 1985, after a presence of 70 years, Royal Dutch Shell decided to end its activities on Curaçao. Shell's announcement came at a crucial moment. The fragile economy of Curaçao had been stagnating for some time. Several revenue-generating endeavours suffered even more during this period: tourism from Venezuela collapsed after the devaluation of the bolivar, the transport industry deteriorated with deleterious effects on the profits of the Antillean Airline Company, and the Curaçao Dry Dock Company experienced major setbacks. The offshore industry (financial services) also experienced a downturn because of new tax laws in the United States.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>In the mid-1980s, Shell sold the refinery for the symbolic amount of one <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antillean_guilder" title="Netherlands Antillean guilder">Antillean guilder</a> to a local government consortium. The aging refinery has been the subject of lawsuits in recent years, which charge that its emissions, including <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_particulate_matter" class="mw-redirect" title="Atmospheric particulate matter">particulate matter</a>, far exceed safety standards.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> The government consortium currently leases the refinery to the Venezuelan state oil company <a href="/wiki/PDVSA" title="PDVSA">PDVSA</a>.
</p><p>Continuing economic hardship in the late 1990s and early 2000s has resulted in emigration to the Netherlands being at high levels.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 1 July 2007, the island of Curaçao was due to become a country within the Kingdom of the Netherlands. On 28 November 2006, this was delayed when the island council rejected a clarification memorandum on the process. A new island council ratified this agreement on 9 July 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-approved_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-approved-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> On 15 December 2008, Curaçao was scheduled to become a separate country within the Kingdom of the Netherlands (as Aruba and the Netherlands Antilles were). A non-binding referendum on this plan took place in Curaçao on 15 May 2009, in which 52% of the voters supported these plans.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Since_the_dissolution_of_the_Netherlands_Antilles">Since the dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Since the dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Netherlands_Antilles" title="Dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles">dissolution of the Netherlands Antilles</a> came into effect on 10 October 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Curaçao became a country within the Kingdom of the Netherlands, with the Kingdom retaining responsibility for defence and foreign policy. The kingdom was also to oversee the island's finances under a debt-relief arrangement agreed between the two.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Curaçao's first <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Prime Minister of Curaçao">prime minister</a> was <a href="/wiki/Gerrit_Schotte" title="Gerrit Schotte">Gerrit Schotte</a>. He was succeeded in 2012 by <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Betrian" title="Stanley Betrian">Stanley Betrian</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Ad_interim" title="Ad interim">ad interim</a></i>. After elections in 2012 <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Hodge" title="Daniel Hodge">Daniel Hodge</a> became the third prime minister, on 31 December 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Hodge_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hodge-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> He led a <a href="/wiki/Demissionary_cabinet" title="Demissionary cabinet">demissionary cabinet</a> until 7 June 2013, when a new cabinet under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Ivar_Asjes" title="Ivar Asjes">Ivar Asjes</a> was sworn in.<sup id="cite_ref-Asjes_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Asjes-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although Curaçao is autonomous, the Netherlands has interfered when necessary to ensure that parliamentary elections were held and to assist in finalizing an accurate budget. In July 2017, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Eugene_Rhuggenaath" title="Eugene Rhuggenaath">Eugene Rhuggenaath</a> stated that he wants the island to take full responsibility, but asked for more cooperation and assistance from the Netherlands with suggestions for more innovative approaches to help Curaçao succeed, increasing the standard of living.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The Dutch government reminded Curaçao that it has provided assistance with oil refinery negotiations with the Chinese "on numerous occasions".<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_populated_places_in_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="List of populated places in Curaçao">List of populated places in Curaçao</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Curacao_Dushi_(34800928041).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Curacao_Dushi_%2834800928041%29.jpg/220px-Curacao_Dushi_%2834800928041%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Curacao_Dushi_%2834800928041%29.jpg/330px-Curacao_Dushi_%2834800928041%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Curacao_Dushi_%2834800928041%29.jpg/440px-Curacao_Dushi_%2834800928041%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3733" data-file-height="2097" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Curacao_Dushi_(34800928041).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of the coast of Curaçao</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Curacao-CIA_WFB_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Curacao-CIA_WFB_Map.png/220px-Curacao-CIA_WFB_Map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a5/Curacao-CIA_WFB_Map.png 1.5x" data-file-width="325" data-file-height="349" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Curacao-CIA_WFB_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of Curaçao</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cura%C3%A7ao_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_2,_left.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Cura%C3%A7ao_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_2%2C_left.gif/220px-Cura%C3%A7ao_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_2%2C_left.gif" decoding="async" width="220" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Cura%C3%A7ao_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_2%2C_left.gif/330px-Cura%C3%A7ao_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_2%2C_left.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Cura%C3%A7ao_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_2%2C_left.gif/440px-Cura%C3%A7ao_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_2%2C_left.gif 2x" data-file-width="3058" data-file-height="2868" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cura%C3%A7ao_-_Encyclopaedie_van_Nederlandsch_West-Indi%C3%AB-Antilles_part_2,_left.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A detailed map of Curaçao from the <i>Encyclopaedie van Nederlandsch West-Indië 1914–1917</i>.</div></div></div>
<p>Curaçao, as well as the rest of the <a href="/wiki/ABC_islands_(Lesser_Antilles)" title="ABC islands (Lesser Antilles)">ABC islands</a> and also <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, lies on the continental shelf of South America. It is a thin island with a generally hilly topography; the highest point is the Mount <a href="/wiki/Christoffelberg" title="Christoffelberg">Christoffelberg</a> 372&#160;m (1,220&#160;ft) in the north-west.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The coastlines bays, inlets and hot springs offer an on-site source of natural mineral, thermal, or seawater used in hydrotherapy and mesotherapy, making this island one of many <a href="/wiki/Balneotherapy" title="Balneotherapy">balneoclimateric</a> areas in the region. Off the south-east coast lies the small, flat island of <a href="/wiki/Klein_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Klein Curaçao">Klein Curaçao</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora">Flora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Flora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The flora of Curaçao differs from the typical tropical island vegetation. <a href="/wiki/Xeric" class="mw-redirect" title="Xeric">Xeric</a> <a href="/wiki/Scrubland" class="mw-redirect" title="Scrubland">scrublands</a> are common, with various forms of <a href="/wiki/Cacti" class="mw-redirect" title="Cacti">cacti</a>, thorny shrubs, <a href="/wiki/Evergreen" title="Evergreen">evergreen</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Watapana" class="mw-redirect" title="Watapana">watapana</a> tree, called <i><a href="/wiki/Divi-divi" class="mw-redirect" title="Divi-divi">divi-divi</a></i> on Aruba, characteristic for the ABC islands and the national symbol of Aruba.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fauna">Fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Rodents_of_the_Caribbean#Curaçao" class="mw-redirect" title="Rodents of the Caribbean">Rodents of the Caribbean §&#160;Curaçao</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Curaçao has a <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>BSh</i>) with a <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry season</a> from January to September and a <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">wet season</a> from October to December.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The temperatures are relatively constant with small differences throughout the year. The <a href="/wiki/Trade_winds" title="Trade winds">trade winds</a> bring cooling during the day and the same trade winds bring warming during the night. The coolest month is January with an average temperature of 26.5&#160;°C (80&#160;°F) and the warmest month is September with an average temperature of 28.9&#160;°C (84&#160;°F). The year's average maximum temperature is 31.2&#160;°C (88&#160;°F). The year's average minimum temperature is 25.3&#160;°C (78&#160;°F).
</p><p>Curaçao lies outside the <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_belt" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane belt">hurricane belt</a>, but is still occasionally affected by hurricanes, as for example <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Hazel" title="Hurricane Hazel">Hazel</a> in 1954, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Anna_(1961)" title="Hurricane Anna (1961)">Anna</a> in 1961, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Felix_(2007)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Felix (2007)">Felix</a> in 2007, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Omar_(2008)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Omar (2008)">Omar</a> in 2008. A <a href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Hurricane" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane">hurricane</a> in Curaçao has not occurred since the United States <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> started tracking hurricanes. Curaçao has, however, been directly affected by pre-hurricane tropical storms several times; the latest which to do so were <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Tomas" title="Hurricane Tomas">Tomas</a> in 2010, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Cesar-Douglas" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Cesar-Douglas">Cesar</a> in 1996, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Joan-Miriam" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Joan-Miriam">Joan-Miriam</a> in 1988, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Cora" title="Hurricane Cora">Cora</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Greta-Olivia" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Greta-Olivia">Greta</a> in 1978, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Edith_(1971)" title="Hurricane Edith (1971)">Edith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irene_(1971)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane Irene (1971)">Irene</a> in 1971, and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Francelia" title="Hurricane Francelia">Francelia</a> in 1969. Tomas brushed Curaçao as a tropical storm, dropping as much as 265&#160;mm (10.4&#160;in) of precipitation on the territory, nearly half of the annual precipitation in one day.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> This made Tomas one of the wettest events in the island's history,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> as well as one of the most devastating; its flooding killed two people and caused over NAƒ60&#160;million (US$28&#160;million) in damage.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Meteo, the Curaçao Weather Department, provides up to date information about weather conditions, via its website and mobile apps for iOS and Android.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The northern sea floor drops steeply within 60&#160;m (200&#160;ft) of the shore. This drop-off is known as the "blue edge".
</p><p>On Curaçao, four major geological formations can be found: the lava formation, the Knip formation, the Mid-Curaçao formation and limestone formations.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Curaçao lies within the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_large_igneous_province" title="Caribbean large igneous province">Caribbean large igneous province</a> (CLIP) with key exposures of those lavas existing on the island consisting of the Curaçao Lava Formation (CLF).  The CLF consists of 5&#160;km of <a href="/wiki/Pillow_lava" title="Pillow lava">pillow lavas</a> with some <a href="/wiki/Basalt" title="Basalt">basalt</a> <a href="/wiki/Intrusion" class="mw-redirect" title="Intrusion">intrusions</a>.  The ages of these rocks include 89 <a href="/wiki/Mega-annum" class="mw-redirect" title="Mega-annum">Ma</a> for the lavas and 75 Ma for the <a href="/wiki/Poikilitic" title="Poikilitic">poikilitic</a> <a href="/wiki/Sill_(geology)" title="Sill (geology)">sills</a>, though some sequences may have erupted as late as 62–66 Ma, placing them in the <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a>.  Their composition includes <a href="/wiki/Picrite" class="mw-redirect" title="Picrite">picrite</a> pillows at the base, followed by <a href="/wiki/Tholeiitic" class="mw-redirect" title="Tholeiitic">tholeiitic</a> lavas, then <a href="/wiki/Hyaloclastite" title="Hyaloclastite">hyaloclastites</a>, then the poikilitic sills.  The CLF was gradually <a href="/wiki/Geologic_uplift" class="mw-redirect" title="Geologic uplift">uplifted</a> until <a href="/wiki/Eocene" title="Eocene">Eocene</a>-<a href="/wiki/Miocene" title="Miocene">Miocene</a> limestone caps formed, before final exposure above sea level. <a href="/wiki/Christoffelberg" title="Christoffelberg">Christoffelberg</a> and the Zevenbergen (Seven Hills) portion of the island have exposures of the Knip <a href="/wiki/Formation_(geology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Formation (geology)">Formation</a>.  This formation includes deepwater deposits of <a href="/wiki/Calcareous" title="Calcareous">calcareous</a> <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">sands</a> and fine <a href="/wiki/Clay" title="Clay">clays</a>, capped by <a href="/wiki/Siliceous" class="mw-redirect" title="Siliceous">siliceous</a> <a href="/wiki/Chert" title="Chert">chert</a> containing <a href="/wiki/Radiolarian" class="mw-redirect" title="Radiolarian">radiolarians</a>.  Middle Curaçao contains <a href="/wiki/Alluvial" class="mw-redirect" title="Alluvial">alluvial</a> soils from eroded CLF and limestone.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forts">Forts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Forts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fort_Nassau,_Curacao.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Fort_Nassau%2C_Curacao.jpg/220px-Fort_Nassau%2C_Curacao.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Fort_Nassau%2C_Curacao.jpg/330px-Fort_Nassau%2C_Curacao.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Fort_Nassau%2C_Curacao.jpg/440px-Fort_Nassau%2C_Curacao.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fort_Nassau,_Curacao.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fort Nassau entrance.</div></div></div>
<p>When the Dutch arrived in 1634, they built forts at key points around the island to protect themselves from foreign powers, privateers, and pirates. Six of the best-preserved forts can still be seen today:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Fort_Amsterdam_(Cura%C3%A7ao)" title="Fort Amsterdam (Curaçao)">Fort Amsterdam</a> (1635)</li>
<li>Fort Beekenburg (1703)</li>
<li>Fort Nassau (1797)</li>
<li>Waterfort (1826)</li>
<li>Riffort (1828)<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Piscadera Bay Fort (built between 1701 and 1704)</li></ul>
<p>In 1957, the Hotel Van der Valk Plaza Curaçao was built on top of the Waterfort.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Riffort contains restaurants and shops. It is located on the opposite side of the Waterfort across the entrance to the harbour in <a href="/wiki/Otrobanda" title="Otrobanda">Otrobanda</a>. In 2009, the Renaissance Curaçao Resort and Casino opened next to the Riffort.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Government of Curaçao">Government of Curaçao</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/220px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/330px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png/440px-EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png 2x" data-file-width="2206" data-file-height="1358" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EU_OCT_and_OMR_map_en.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the European Union in the world with <a href="/wiki/Special_member_state_territories_and_the_European_Union" title="Special member state territories and the European Union">overseas countries and territories and outermost regions</a></div></div></div>
<p>Curaçao is a constituent country of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Its governance takes place in a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a>. The <a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="King of the Netherlands">King of the Netherlands</a> is the head of state, represented locally by a <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Governor of Curaçao">Governor</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Prime Minister of Curaçao">Prime Minister of Curaçao</a> being the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government. <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Legislative power">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the government and <a href="/wiki/Estates_of_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Estates of Curaçao">parliament</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a> is independent of the executive and the legislature. Convicted felons are held at the <a href="/wiki/Sentro_di_Detenshon_i_Korekshon_K%C3%B2rsou" class="mw-redirect" title="Sentro di Detenshon i Korekshon Kòrsou">Curaçao Centre for Detention and Correction</a> prison.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Curaçao has full autonomy on most matters, with the exceptions summed up in the <a href="/wiki/Charter_for_the_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Charter for the Kingdom of the Netherlands">Charter for the Kingdom of the Netherlands</a> under the title "<a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands#Kingdom_affairs" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom affairs</a>".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luchtfoto_van_de_marinebasis_Parera_op_Cura%C3%A7ao.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Luchtfoto_van_de_marinebasis_Parera_op_Cura%C3%A7ao.jpg/220px-Luchtfoto_van_de_marinebasis_Parera_op_Cura%C3%A7ao.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Luchtfoto_van_de_marinebasis_Parera_op_Cura%C3%A7ao.jpg/330px-Luchtfoto_van_de_marinebasis_Parera_op_Cura%C3%A7ao.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Luchtfoto_van_de_marinebasis_Parera_op_Cura%C3%A7ao.jpg/440px-Luchtfoto_van_de_marinebasis_Parera_op_Cura%C3%A7ao.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2784" data-file-height="1848" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luchtfoto_van_de_marinebasis_Parera_op_Cura%C3%A7ao.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Parera Naval Base</div></div></div>
<p>Defence of the island is the responsibility of the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Two <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Navy" title="Royal Netherlands Navy">Dutch</a> naval bases, Parera and Suffisant, are located on the island of Curaçao. Officers of the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Aruba" title="Military of Aruba">Arubaanse Militie</a> complete further training on Curaçao.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>On the west side of <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_International_Airport" title="Curaçao International Airport">Curaçao International Airport</a> are hangars for the two Bombardier Dash 8 Maritime Patrol Aircraft and two AgustaWestland AW139 helicopters of the Dutch Caribbean Coast Guard. This was until 2007 a naval airbase of the Royal Netherlands Navy, which operated the base for 55 years, with a wide variety of aircraft in the past years Fireflies, Avengers, Trackers, Neptunes, Fokker F-27's, P-3C Orions, Fokker F-60's and several helicopters. After the political decision to sell all Orions the airbase wasn't needed anymore.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>The west end of the airport is a <a href="/wiki/USAF" class="mw-redirect" title="USAF">USAF</a> <a href="/wiki/Forward_Operating_Site" title="Forward Operating Site">Forward Operating Location</a> (FOL). The base hosts AWACS and transport aircraft. Until 1999 the USAF operated a small fleet of F-16 fighters from the FOB.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Conscription">Conscription</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Conscription">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Suffisant Naval Base has facilities used for conscription in the Caribbean. There has not been military conscription since 1997, but a form of civil conscription has been in place. This type of conscription offers underprivileged Antillean young people the chance of undertaking professional training.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b>The politics of Curaçao</b> reflect a nation that has experienced conflict between its two major <a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">immigrant</a> groups. One represents immigrants from the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, now a small minority, the other descendants of <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Africa" title="Slavery in Africa">African slaves</a>, well into the majority. In 2010 Curaçao became an autonomous country as part of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>. Until that election the island country in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> was part of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</a>. <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a> island also became autonomous, while the less-populated islands of <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sint_Eustatius" title="Sint Eustatius">Sint Eustatius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a> are cities governed by the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><br />
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Economy of Curaçao">Economy of Curaçao</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bohrinsel_Curacao_(34800864151).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Bohrinsel_Curacao_%2834800864151%29.jpg/220px-Bohrinsel_Curacao_%2834800864151%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Bohrinsel_Curacao_%2834800864151%29.jpg/330px-Bohrinsel_Curacao_%2834800864151%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Bohrinsel_Curacao_%2834800864151%29.jpg/440px-Bohrinsel_Curacao_%2834800864151%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3992" data-file-height="2242" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bohrinsel_Curacao_(34800864151).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Offshore Oil platform in Curaçao</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Historic_Area_of_Willemstad,_Inner_City_and_Harbour,_Cura%C3%A7ao-139159.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139159.jpg/220px-Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139159.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139159.jpg/330px-Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139159.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139159.jpg/440px-Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139159.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Historic_Area_of_Willemstad,_Inner_City_and_Harbour,_Cura%C3%A7ao-139159.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Historic Area of Willemstad, declared <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> by UNESCO in 1997.</div></div></div>
<p>Curaçao has an <a href="/wiki/Open_economy" title="Open economy">open economy</a>, with tourism, international trade, shipping services, oil refining,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> storage (oil and bunkering) and international financial services being the most important sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The Venezuelan state oil company <a href="/wiki/PDVSA" title="PDVSA">PDVSA</a> has a lease on the island's oil refinery expiring in 2019; the facility employs 1,000 people, refining oil from <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> for export to the US and Asia.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Schlumberger" title="Schlumberger">Schlumberger</a>, the world's largest oil field services company is incorporated in Curaçao.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Isla_oil_refinery&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Isla oil refinery (page does not exist)">Isla oil refinery</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raffinerie_de_Isla" class="extiw" title="fr:Raffinerie de Isla">fr</a>; <a href="https://nl.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isla_(raffinaderij)" class="extiw" title="nl:Isla (raffinaderij)">nl</a>&#93;</span> is claimed to be responsible for Curaçao's position in the world's top five highest countries for CO2 emissions per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Along with <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a>, Curaçao uses the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antillean_guilder" title="Netherlands Antillean guilder">Netherlands Antillean guilder</a> as its currency.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Its economy is well developed, supporting a high standard of living, ranking 46th in the world in terms of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">GDP (PPP) per capita</a> and 27th in the world in terms of <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">nominal GDP per capita</a>. Curaçao possesses a <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">high income economy</a>, as defined by the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Activities related to the port of Willemstad (like the <a href="/wiki/Free_Trade_Zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Free Trade Zone">Free Trade Zone</a>) make a significant contribution to the economy.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> To achieve the government's aim to make its economy more diverse, efforts are being made to attract more foreign investment.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> This policy, called the "Open Arms" policy, features a heavy focus on information technology companies.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Reduced foreign demand due to ongoing unrest and political uncertainty in Venezuela has led to decreased exports along with increased public demands for services and goods which has resulted in economic stagnation since 2016. Expansion was recorded in the construction, financial intermediation, and utilities sectors while other aspects of the economy contracted.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Curacao_Jan_Thiel_(34526956140).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Curacao_Jan_Thiel_%2834526956140%29.jpg/220px-Curacao_Jan_Thiel_%2834526956140%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Curacao_Jan_Thiel_%2834526956140%29.jpg/330px-Curacao_Jan_Thiel_%2834526956140%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Curacao_Jan_Thiel_%2834526956140%29.jpg/440px-Curacao_Jan_Thiel_%2834526956140%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3992" data-file-height="2242" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Curacao_Jan_Thiel_(34526956140).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Jan Thiel beach Curaçao</div></div></div>
<p>While tourism plays a major role in Curaçao's economy, it is less reliant on tourism than other Caribbean countries. Most tourists originate from the Netherlands, the eastern United States, South America and other Caribbean Islands.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> It is a leader in the Caribbean in cruise tourism growth with 610,186 cruise passengers in 2013, a 41.4% increase over the prior year.<sup id="cite_ref-CaribbeanInTourismGrowth_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CaribbeanInTourismGrowth-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hato_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Hato International Airport">Hato International Airport</a> received 1,772,501 passengers in 2013 and recently announced capital investments totaling US$48&#160;million aimed at transforming the airport into a regional hub by 2018.
</p><p>The island's <a href="/wiki/Continental_shelf" title="Continental shelf">insular shelf</a> has a sharp drop-off known as the "Blue Edge" which is often visited by <a href="/wiki/Scuba_diving" title="Scuba diving">scuba diving</a> tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> Coral reefs for <a href="/wiki/Snorkeling" title="Snorkeling">snorkeling</a> and scuba diving can be reached without a boat. The southern coast has calm waters as well as many small beaches, such as Jan Thiel and Cas Abou. The coastline of Curaçao features numerous bays and inlets which serve as popular mooring locations for boats.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2017, the island was named the Top Cruise Destination in the Southern Caribbean by <a href="/wiki/Cruise_Critic" title="Cruise Critic">Cruise Critic</a>, a major online forum. The winners of the Destination Awards were selected based on comments from cruise passengers who rated the downtown area of Willemstad as "amazing" and the food and shopping as "excellent".<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some of the coral reefs are affected by tourism. <a href="/wiki/Playa_Porto_Marie" title="Playa Porto Marie">Porto Marie Beach</a> is experimenting with artificial coral reefs in order to improve the reef's condition.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Hundreds of artificial coral blocks that have been placed are now home to a large array of tropical fish. It is now under investigation to see if the sewer waste of hotels is a partial cause of the dying of the coral reef.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Curacao-Sea-Aquarium-2013.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Curacao-Sea-Aquarium-2013.JPG/220px-Curacao-Sea-Aquarium-2013.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Curacao-Sea-Aquarium-2013.JPG/330px-Curacao-Sea-Aquarium-2013.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Curacao-Sea-Aquarium-2013.JPG/440px-Curacao-Sea-Aquarium-2013.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4573" data-file-height="2865" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Curacao-Sea-Aquarium-2013.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Curaçao Sea Aquarium and the Dolphin Academy share this islet on the west coast of Curaçao, with <a href="/wiki/Seaquarium_Beach" title="Seaquarium Beach">Seaquarium Beach</a> nearby.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Labour">Labour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Labour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2016, a Labor Force Survey (LFS) indicated that the unemployment rate was 13.3%. For residents aged 15–64, the employment rate was 70.4%.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_services">Financial services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Financial services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Curaçao's history in <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a> dates back to <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. Prior to this period, the financial arms of local merchant houses functioned as informal lenders to the community. However, at the turn of the 20th century, Curaçao underwent industrialization, and a number of merchant houses established private <a href="/wiki/Commercial_bank" title="Commercial bank">commercial banks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> As the economy grew, these banks began assuming additional functions eventually becoming full-fledged financial institutions.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Caribbean_Securities_Exchange" title="Dutch Caribbean Securities Exchange">Dutch Caribbean Securities Exchange</a> is located in the capital of Willemstad, as is the <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Cura%C3%A7ao_and_Sint_Maarten" title="Central Bank of Curaçao and Sint Maarten">Central Bank of Curaçao and Sint Maarten</a>; the latter of which dates to 1828. It is the oldest <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a> in the Western Hemisphere.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The island's legal system supports a variety of corporate structures and is a <a href="/wiki/Corporate_haven" title="Corporate haven">corporate haven</a>. Though Curaçao is considered a <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a>, it adheres to the EU Code of Conduct against harmful tax practices. It holds a qualified intermediary status from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Internal_Revenue_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Internal Revenue Service">United States Internal Revenue Service</a>. It is an accepted jurisdiction of the <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">OECD</a> and Caribbean <a href="/wiki/Financial_Action_Task_Force_on_Money_Laundering" title="Financial Action Task Force on Money Laundering">Financial Action Task Force on Money Laundering</a>. The country enforces Anti-<a href="/wiki/Money_Laundering" class="mw-redirect" title="Money Laundering">Money Laundering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Counter-Terrorism" class="mw-redirect" title="Counter-Terrorism">Counter-Terrorism</a> funding compliance.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_Account_Tax_Compliance_Act">Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Historic_Area_of_Willemstad,_Inner_City_and_Harbour,_Cura%C3%A7ao-139160.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139160.jpg/220px-Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139160.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139160.jpg/330px-Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139160.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139160.jpg/440px-Historic_Area_of_Willemstad%2C_Inner_City_and_Harbour%2C_Cura%C3%A7ao-139160.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Historic_Area_of_Willemstad,_Inner_City_and_Harbour,_Cura%C3%A7ao-139160.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Banco di Caribe at Willemstad</div></div></div>
<p>On 30 June 2014, Curaçao<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> was deemed to have an Inter-Governmental Agreement (IGA) with the United States of America with respect to the "Foreign Account Tax Compliance Act" of the United States of America.  The Tax Information Exchange Agreement signed in Washington, D.C. on 17 April 2002<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> between the U.S. and the Kingdom of the Netherlands includes Curaçao, and was updated with respect to Curaco in 2014, taking effect in 2016.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trade">Trade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Trade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Curaçao trades mainly with the United States, Venezuela, and the European Union. It has an Association Agreement with the European Union which allows companies which do business in and via Curaçao to export products to European markets,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> free of import duties and quotas. It is also a participant in the US <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Basin_Initiative" title="Caribbean Basin Initiative">Caribbean Basin Initiative</a> allowing it to have preferential access to the US market.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prostitution">Prostitution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Prostitution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_the_Dutch_Caribbean#Curacao" title="Prostitution in the Dutch Caribbean">Prostitution in the Dutch Caribbean §&#160;Curacao</a></div>
<p>Prostitution in Curaçao is legal only for foreign women who get a temporary permit to work in the large open-air brothel called "Le Mirage" or "<a href="/wiki/Campo_Alegre_(brothel)" title="Campo Alegre (brothel)">Campo Alegre</a>." Using prostitution services is legal for men (locals included). The brothel has operated near the airport since the 1940s.<sup id="cite_ref-chron_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chron-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nswp_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nswp-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> Curaçao monitors, contains and regulates the industry. The government states that the workers in these establishments are thereby given a safe environment and access to medical practitioners. However this approach does exclude local women (or men) to legally make a living from prostitution and does lead to loss of local income, as the foreign prostitutes send or take most of their earnings home.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">U.S. State Department</a> has cited anecdotal evidence claiming that, "Curaçao...[is a] destination island... for women trafficked for the sex trade from Peru, Brazil, Colombia, the Dominican Republic, and Haiti, according to local observers. At least 500 foreign women reportedly are in prostitution throughout the five islands of the Antilles, some of whom have been trafficked."<sup id="cite_ref-trafficking192_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trafficking192-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The US Department of State has said that the government of Curaçao frequently underestimates the extent of <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">human trafficking</a> problems.<sup id="cite_ref-trafficking192_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trafficking192-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cura%C3%A7ao_synagogue1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Cura%C3%A7ao_synagogue1.jpg/220px-Cura%C3%A7ao_synagogue1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Cura%C3%A7ao_synagogue1.jpg/330px-Cura%C3%A7ao_synagogue1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Cura%C3%A7ao_synagogue1.jpg/440px-Cura%C3%A7ao_synagogue1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1944" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cura%C3%A7ao_synagogue1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Mikv%C3%A9_Israel-Emanuel_Synagogue" class="mw-redirect" title="Mikvé Israel-Emanuel Synagogue">Mikvé Israel-Emanuel Synagogue</a> in Willemstad is the oldest-surviving synagogue in the Western hemisphere</div></div></div>
<p>Owing to the island's history of slavery, most Curaçaoans are of <a href="/wiki/Afro-Cura%C3%A7aoan" title="Afro-Curaçaoan">Black African descent</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> There are also sizeable minorities of <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Latin_Americans" title="Latin Americans">Latin Americans</a>, French, South Asians, East Asians, <a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Levant" title="Levant">Levantine</a> Arab people. Additionally, there are both <a href="/wiki/Sephardic" class="mw-redirect" title="Sephardic">Sephardic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi" class="mw-redirect" title="Ashkenazi">Ashkenazi</a> Jewish communities.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="PieChartTemplate thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px">
<div style="background-color:white;margin:auto;position:relative;width:200px;height:200px;overflow:hidden;border-radius:100px;border:1px solid black">
