<div class="thumbcaption">
<dl><dt>Religion in Curaçao<sup id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup></dt></dl>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Roman Catholic (72.8%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:SkyBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Protestant (16.7%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Black; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;None (6%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:grey; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Other (Jewish, Hindu, Muslim, etc.) (3.8%)</div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:LightGrey; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Unspecified (0.6%)</div>
</div>
</div></div>
<p>The religious breakdown of the population of Curaçao, according to a 2011 estimate:<sup id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_105-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> 72.8%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pentecostal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_105-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> 6.6%</li>
<li>Other <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_105-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> 3.2%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Adventism" title="Adventism">Adventist</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_105-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> 3%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_105-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> 2%</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_105-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> 1.9%</li>
<li>Other;<sup id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_105-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> 3.8%</li>
<li>None;<sup id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_105-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> 6%</li>
<li>Unspecified;<sup id="cite_ref-CIACuraçao_105-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIACuraçao-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> 0.6%</li></ul>
<p>This includes a shift towards the charismatic renewal or charismatic movement since the mid-1970s.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Other denominations include the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist Church">Methodist Church</a>. Alongside these Christian denominations, some inhabitants practice <a href="/wiki/Montamentu" title="Montamentu">Montamentu</a> and other diaspora African religions.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> As elsewhere in Latin America, Pentecostalism is on the rise.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> There are also practising Muslims and Hindus.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Willemstad" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Willemstad">Roman Catholic Diocese of Willemstad</a> encompasses all the territory of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> which includes <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a>, Curaçao, <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a>, and the islands of <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._Eustatius" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Eustatius">St. Eustatius</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saba" title="Saba">Saba</a>. The diocese is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Antilles_Episcopal_Conference" title="Antilles Episcopal Conference">Antilles Episcopal Conference</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>While small, Curaçao's <a href="/wiki/Jewish" class="mw-redirect" title="Jewish">Jewish</a> community has had a significant impact on the island's history.<sup id="cite_ref-history_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> Curaçao has the oldest active Jewish congregation in the Americas, dating to 1651. The <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_synagogue" title="Curaçao synagogue">Curaçao synagogue</a> is the oldest synagogue of the Americas in continuous use, since its completion in 1732 on the site of a previous synagogue.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Curaçao is a <a href="/wiki/Multilingualism" title="Multilingualism">polyglot</a> society. The official languages are <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papiamentu" class="mw-redirect" title="Papiamentu">Papiamentu</a> and English.<sup id="cite_ref-official-spanish_portugues,languages_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-official-spanish_portugues,languages-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> However, Dutch is the sole language for all administration and legal matters.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Most of Curaçao's population is able to converse in at least two of the languages of Papiamentu, Dutch, English, and Spanish.
</p><p>The most widely spoken language is Papiamentu, a Portuguese creole with African, Dutch and Spanish influences, spoken in all levels of society.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Papiamentu was introduced as a language of primary school education in 1993, making Curaçao one of a handful of places where a creole language is used as a medium to acquire basic literacy.<sup id="cite_ref-Liddicoat2007_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liddicoat2007-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
Spanish and English also have a long historical presence in Curaçao. Spanish became an important language in the 18th century due to the close economic ties with Spanish colonies in what are now Venezuela and Colombia<sup id="cite_ref-Putte_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Putte-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> and several Venezuelan TV networks are received. Use of English dates to the early 19th century, when the British took Curaçao, Aruba and <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a>. When Dutch rule resumed in 1815, officials already noted wide use of the language.<sup id="cite_ref-Putte_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Putte-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the 2001 census, Papiamentu is the <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">first language</a> of 81.2% of the population. Dutch is the first language of 8%, Spanish of 4%, and English of 2.9%.<sup id="cite_ref-cbs_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbs-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> However, these numbers divide the population in terms of first language and do not account for the high rate of <a href="/wiki/Bilingualism" class="mw-redirect" title="Bilingualism">bilingualism</a> in the population of Curaçao.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hoofdingang_van_de_University_of_Curacao-Mei_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Hoofdingang_van_de_University_of_Curacao-Mei_2018.jpg/220px-Hoofdingang_van_de_University_of_Curacao-Mei_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Hoofdingang_van_de_University_of_Curacao-Mei_2018.jpg/330px-Hoofdingang_van_de_University_of_Curacao-Mei_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Hoofdingang_van_de_University_of_Curacao-Mei_2018.jpg/440px-Hoofdingang_van_de_University_of_Curacao-Mei_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hoofdingang_van_de_University_of_Curacao-Mei_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The University of Curaçao</div></div></div>
<p>Public education is based on the Dutch educational system and besides the public schools, private and parochial schools are also available. Since the introduction of a new public education law in 1992, compulsory primary education starts at age six and continues for six years; secondary lasts for another four.<sup id="cite_ref-edu_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edu-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The main institute of higher learning is the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cura%C3%A7ao" title="University of Curaçao">University of Curaçao</a>, enrolling 2,100 students.<sup id="cite_ref-edu_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-edu-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> The comprehensive model of education is influenced by both the Dutch and American education systems. Other higher education offerings on the island include <a href="/wiki/Offshore_Medical_School_in_the_Caribbean" class="mw-redirect" title="Offshore Medical School in the Caribbean">offshore medical schools</a>, language schools and academies for fine art, music, police, teacher and nurse-training.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bulawaya-1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Bulawaya-1.jpg/220px-Bulawaya-1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="194" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Bulawaya-1.jpg/330px-Bulawaya-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Bulawaya-1.jpg/440px-Bulawaya-1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2014" data-file-height="1780" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bulawaya-1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Bulawaya dance</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Despite the island's relatively small population, the diversity of languages and cultural influences on Curaçao have generated a remarkable literary tradition, primarily in <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Papiamentu" class="mw-redirect" title="Papiamentu">Papiamentu</a>. The oral traditions of the <a href="/wiki/Arawak_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Arawak peoples">Arawak</a> <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous peoples</a> are lost. West African slaves brought the tales of <a href="/wiki/Anansi" title="Anansi">Anansi</a>, thus forming the basis of Papiamentu literature. The first published work in Papiamentu was a poem by Joseph Sickman Corsen entitled <i>Atardi</i>, published in the <i>La Cruz</i> newspaper in 1905.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Throughout Curaçaoan literature, narrative techniques and metaphors best characterized as <a href="/wiki/Magic_realism" title="Magic realism">magic realism</a> tend to predominate.  Novelists and poets from Curaçao have contributed to <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean Literature">Caribbean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_literature" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch literature">Dutch literature</a>.  Best known are <a href="/wiki/Cola_Debrot" title="Cola Debrot">Cola Debrot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Martinus_Arion" title="Frank Martinus Arion">Frank Martinus Arion</a>, Pierre Lauffer, Elis Juliana, Guillermo Rosario, Boeli van Leeuwen and <a href="/wiki/Tip_Marugg" title="Tip Marugg">Tip Marugg</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Local food is called <i>Krioyo</i> (pronounced the same as <i>criollo</i>, the Spanish word for "Creole") and boasts a blend of flavours and techniques best compared to Caribbean cuisine and Latin American cuisine. Dishes common in Curaçao are found in <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bonaire" title="Bonaire">Bonaire</a> as well. Popular dishes include: stobá (a stew made with various ingredients such as <a href="/wiki/Papaya" title="Papaya">papaya</a>, beef or goat), Guiambo (soup made from <a href="/wiki/Okra" title="Okra">okra</a> and seafood), kadushi (cactus soup), sopi mondongo (intestine soup), funchi (cornmeal paste similar to <a href="/wiki/Fufu" title="Fufu">fufu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ugali" title="Ugali">ugali</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polenta" title="Polenta">polenta</a>) and a lot of fish and other seafood. The ubiquitous side dish is fried <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantain (cooking)">plantain</a>. Local bread rolls are made according to a Portuguese recipe. All around the island, there are snèks which serve local dishes as well as alcoholic drinks in a manner akin to the English <a href="/wiki/Public_house" class="mw-redirect" title="Public house">public house</a>.
</p><p>The ubiquitous breakfast dish is pastechi: fried pastry with fillings of cheese, tuna, ham, or ground meat. Around the holiday season special dishes are consumed, such as the <a href="/wiki/Hallaca" title="Hallaca">hallaca</a> and pekelé, made out of <a href="/wiki/Salt_cod" class="mw-redirect" title="Salt cod">salt cod</a>. At weddings and other special occasions a variety of kos dushi are served: kokada (coconut sweets), ko'i lechi (condensed milk and sugar sweet) and tentalaria (peanut sweets). The <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_liqueur" class="mw-redirect" title="Curaçao liqueur">Curaçao liqueur</a> was developed here, when a local experimented with the rinds of the local <a href="/wiki/Citrus" title="Citrus">citrus</a> fruit known as <a href="/wiki/Laraha" title="Laraha">laraha</a>. <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Surinamese</a>, Chinese, Indonesian, Indian and Dutch culinary influences also abound. The island also has a number of Chinese restaurants that serve mainly Indonesian dishes such as <a href="/wiki/Satay" title="Satay">satay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nasi_goreng" title="Nasi goreng">nasi goreng</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lumpia" title="Lumpia">lumpia</a> (which are all Indonesian names for the dishes). Dutch specialties such as <a href="/wiki/Croquette" title="Croquette">croquettes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oliebollen" class="mw-redirect" title="Oliebollen">oliebollen</a> are widely served in homes and restaurants.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_national_football_team" title="Curaçao national football team">Curaçao national football team</a> travelled to <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> and participated in the <a href="/wiki/2019_King%27s_Cup" title="2019 King&#39;s Cup">2019 King's Cup</a> for the first time, eventually winning the tournament by beating <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> in the final.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jurickson_Profar_(9260642222).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Jurickson_Profar_%289260642222%29.jpg/220px-Jurickson_Profar_%289260642222%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="312" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Jurickson_Profar_%289260642222%29.jpg/330px-Jurickson_Profar_%289260642222%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Jurickson_Profar_%289260642222%29.jpg/440px-Jurickson_Profar_%289260642222%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1507" data-file-height="2139" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jurickson_Profar_(9260642222).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jurickson_Profar" title="Jurickson Profar">Jurickson Profar</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/Little_League_Baseball" title="Little League Baseball">Little League Baseball</a> team from Willemstad, Curaçao, won the world title in a game against the United States champion from <a href="/wiki/Thousand_Oaks,_California" title="Thousand Oaks, California">Thousand Oaks, California</a>. The Willemstad lineup included <a href="/wiki/Jurickson_Profar" title="Jurickson Profar">Jurickson Profar</a>, the standout shortstop prospect who now plays for the <a href="/wiki/Oakland_Athletics" title="Oakland Athletics">Oakland Athletics</a> of <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Schoop" title="Jonathan Schoop">Jonathan Schoop</a>, who now plays for the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Twins" title="Minnesota Twins">Minnesota Twins</a>.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/2006_World_Baseball_Classic" title="2006 World Baseball Classic">2006 World Baseball Classic</a>, Curaçaoans played for the Netherlands team. <a href="/wiki/Shairon_Martis" title="Shairon Martis">Shairon Martis</a>, born in <a href="/wiki/Willemstad" title="Willemstad">Willemstad</a>, contributed to the Dutch team by throwing a seven-inning no-hitter against Panama (the game was stopped due to the <a href="/wiki/Mercy_rule" title="Mercy rule">mercy rule</a>).
</p><p>The 2010 documentary film, <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=Boys_of_Summer_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Boys of Summer (film) (page does not exist)">Boys of Summer</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> details Curaçao's Pabao Little League All-Stars winning their country's eighth straight championship at the 2008 Little League World Series, then going on to defeat other teams, including Puerto Rico and the Dominican Republic, and earning a spot in Williamsport.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Marc_de_Maar" title="Marc de Maar">Marc de Maar</a> is the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Road_and_Track_Championships" title="Pan American Road and Track Championships">Pan American Road Cycling</a> Champion and has also represented Curaçao at the world cycling championships
</p><p>The prevailing trade winds and warm water make Curaçao a location for windsurfing.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> One factor is that the deep water around Curaçao makes it difficult to lay marks for major windsurfing events, thus hindering the island's success as a windsurfing destination.
</p><p>Kitesurfing or kiteboarding is also loved on Curaçao. The spot for kiteboarding is located at the St. Joris Bay, past the Ostrich Farm.
</p><p>There is warm, clear water around the island. Scuba divers and snorkelers may have visibility up to 30 metres (98 feet) at the Curaçao Underwater Marine Park, which stretches along 20 kilometres (12 miles) of Curaçao's southern coastline.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Curaçao participated in the <a href="/wiki/2013_CARIFTA_Games" title="2013 CARIFTA Games">2013 CARIFTA Games</a>. Kevin Philbert stood third in the under-20 male Long Jump with a distance of 7.36 metres (24.15 feet). Vanessa Philbert stood second the under-17 female 1,500 metres (4,900 feet) with a time of 4:47.97.<sup id="cite_ref-cfpi_1_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfpi_1-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-milesplit_1_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-milesplit_1-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cfpi_2_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfpi_2-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-milesplit_2_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-milesplit_2-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Iv%C3%A1n_Samuco" title="Iván Samuco">Iván Samuco</a> is one of Curacao's most noted professional <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxers</a>, having held the <a href="/wiki/World_Boxing_Council" title="World Boxing Council">World Boxing Council</a>'s Fecarbox Super-Featherweight title and unsuccessfully fought <a href="/wiki/Wilfredo_Gomez" class="mw-redirect" title="Wilfredo Gomez">Wilfredo Gomez</a>.
</p><p>One of the island's most notable footballing exports, is <a href="/wiki/Cuco_Martina" title="Cuco Martina">Cuco Martina</a>. The right sided defender has enjoyed a career throughout Europe, playing for teams such as <a href="/wiki/FC_Twente" title="FC Twente">Twente</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southampton_F.C." title="Southampton F.C.">Southampton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Everton_F.C." title="Everton F.C.">Everton</a>. Dutch born Martina has amassed 42 caps for Curacao to date. 
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport">Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao_International_Airport" title="Curaçao International Airport">Curaçao International Airport</a> (also called Hato International Airport) is located on the northern coast of the island and offers connections to the Caribbean region, South America, North America and Europe. Curaçao Airport is a fairly large facility, with the third longest commercial runway in the Caribbean region after Rafael Hernández Airport in Puerto Rico and Pointe-à-Pitre International Airport in Guadeloupe. The airport served as a main base for <a href="/wiki/Insel_Air" title="Insel Air">Insel Air</a>, and for <a href="/wiki/Air_ALM" class="mw-redirect" title="Air ALM">Air ALM</a>, the former national airlines of Curaçao.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bridges">Bridges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Bridges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Curacao-Bridges-2013.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Curacao-Bridges-2013.JPG/220px-Curacao-Bridges-2013.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Curacao-Bridges-2013.JPG/330px-Curacao-Bridges-2013.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Curacao-Bridges-2013.JPG/440px-Curacao-Bridges-2013.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3130" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Curacao-Bridges-2013.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Queen_Emma_Bridge" title="Queen Emma Bridge">Queen Emma</a> (semi-open), and the <a href="/wiki/Queen_Juliana_Bridge" title="Queen Juliana Bridge">Queen Juliana</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Smith_brug_over_the_Waaigat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Smith_brug_over_the_Waaigat.jpg/220px-Smith_brug_over_the_Waaigat.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Smith_brug_over_the_Waaigat.jpg/330px-Smith_brug_over_the_Waaigat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Smith_brug_over_the_Waaigat.jpg/440px-Smith_brug_over_the_Waaigat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Smith_brug_over_the_Waaigat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Smith brug over the Waaigat</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kon._Wilhelmina_brug_over_the_Waaigat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Kon._Wilhelmina_brug_over_the_Waaigat.jpg/220px-Kon._Wilhelmina_brug_over_the_Waaigat.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Kon._Wilhelmina_brug_over_the_Waaigat.jpg/330px-Kon._Wilhelmina_brug_over_the_Waaigat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Kon._Wilhelmina_brug_over_the_Waaigat.jpg/440px-Kon._Wilhelmina_brug_over_the_Waaigat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kon._Wilhelmina_brug_over_the_Waaigat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Kon. Wilhelmina brug over the Waaigat</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Queen_Emma_Bridge" title="Queen Emma Bridge">Queen Emma Bridge</a>, a 168 metres (551&#160;ft) long <a href="/wiki/Pontoon_bridge" title="Pontoon bridge">pontoon bridge</a>, connects pedestrians between the Punda and Otrobanda districts.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> This swings open to allow the passage of ships to and from the port.<sup id="cite_ref-queen_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-queen-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> The bridge was originally opened in 1888 and the current bridge was installed in 1939.<sup id="cite_ref-emmabridge_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emmabridge-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> It is best known and, more often than not, referred to by the locals as "Our Swinging Old Lady".<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Queen_Juliana_Bridge" title="Queen Juliana Bridge">Queen Juliana Bridge</a> connects mobile traffic between the same two districts. At 185 feet (56&#160;m) above the sea, it is one of the highest bridges in the Caribbean.<sup id="cite_ref-queen_127-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-queen-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Utilities_and_sanitation">Utilities and sanitation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Utilities and sanitation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Aqualectra, a government-owned company<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> and full member of <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Electric_Utility_Services_Corporation_(CARILEC)" class="mw-redirect" title="Caribbean Electric Utility Services Corporation (CARILEC)">CARILEC</a>, delivers potable water and electricity to the island. Rates are controlled by the government. Water is produced by <a href="/wiki/Reverse_osmosis" title="Reverse osmosis">reverse osmosis</a> or <a href="/wiki/Desalinization" class="mw-redirect" title="Desalinization">desalinization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aqualectra.com_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aqualectra.com-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> It services 69,000 households and companies using 130,000 water and electric meters.<sup id="cite_ref-aqualectra.com_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aqualectra.com-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>  The power generation company NuCuraçao opened wind farms in Tera Kora and Playa Kanoa in 2012, and expanded in Tera Kora in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> There is no natural gas distribution grid; gas is supplied to homes by pressurized containers.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Curbside trash pickup is provided by the company Selikor.  There is no recycling pickup, but there are drop-off centers for certain recycled materials at the Malpais landfill,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> and various locations operated by Green Force;<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> private haulers recycle construction waste, paper, and cardboard.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_residents">Notable residents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Notable residents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cura%C3%A7ao&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Politics and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
